Proof that God precedes the world by an infinite duration
Sanusi proves that if the world is created, God precedes it by an infinite duration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand a rational proof that if the world is created, God must precede it by an infinite duration, and why this priority is not merely a finite period.

Core Idea
God's priority over the world is not finite but infinite in duration.

Sanusi presents a logical proof to demonstrate that God's existence before the world is not limited to any finite period. By considering measurable durations like one thousand and two thousand years, he shows that the priority must be infinite if the world is originated. This argument relies on the intuitive understanding of duration as something that can be compared and extended.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Get a feel for the author's argument.
2
Understand the initial premise
The passage begins by asserting that since God exists eternally and the world does not, God must be prior to the world. Make sure you see why this is a necessary conclusion.
Eternity (al-azal) means existence without beginning.
3
Follow the thought experiment
Sanusi asks you to imagine God existing one thousand years before the world, and also two thousand years before. Notice that the priority is greater in the second case, and that this increase is real, not just assumed.
The argument uses a simple comparison to show that priority can be measured.
4
Grasp the conclusion
From the measurable increase, Sanusi concludes that if the world is created, God's priority is infinite. See why the logic forces this: there is no cap on how much priority can be extended.
The conclusion is that God's priority is not a finite duration but infinite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه : هو أن البارى تعالى ، لما كان موجوداً في الأزل ، وما كان العالم موجوداً في الأزل ، لزم القطع بكون البارى تعالى متقدماً على العالم . ثم نقول : لا شك أن البارى تعالى ، كان موجوداً قبل حدوث العالم بتقدير ألف سنة . وكان أيضاً موجوداً قبل حدوث العالم بتقدير ألفي سنة . ولا شك أن التقدم الحاصل على أول العالم بتقدير ألفي سنة ، أزيد مقداراً من التقدم الحاصل على أول العالم بألف سنة . وهذه الزيادة ليست بمجرد فرضنا واعتبارنا ، لأن كل ما لا حصول له إلا بحسب الفرض والاعتبار ، كان واجب التغير، بحسب تغير الفرض والاعتبار . ونحن بالبديهة تعلم: أن القدر الذي به يحصل التقدم على أول العالم ، بمقدار ألفي سنة : ضعف الذي به يحصل التقدم على أول العالم بألف سنة . ولا معنى للمدة والزمان إلا هذا المقدار ، القابل للمساواة والمقارنة ، فيثبت : أنه لو كان العالم محدثاً ، لكان البارىء متقدماً عليه بمدة غير متناهية .
Upon it: [The proof] is that the Creator, exalted, since He was existent in eternity, and the world was not existent in eternity, it is necessary to conclude that the Creator, exalted, is prior to the world. Then we say: There is no doubt that the Creator, exalted, was existent before the occurrence of the world by an estimated thousand years. And He was also existent before the occurrence of the world by an estimated two thousand years. And there is no doubt that the priority obtained over the beginning of the world by two thousand years is greater in measure than the priority obtained over the beginning of the world by one thousand years. And this increase is not merely by our assumption and consideration, because everything that has no existence except in accordance with assumption and consideration would necessarily change according to the change of assumption and consideration. And we know by intuition that the amount by which priority over the beginning of the world of two thousand years is obtained is double that by which priority over the beginning of the world of one thousand years is obtained. And there is no meaning of duration and time except this amount, which is susceptible to equality and comparison. So it is established that if the world were originated, the Creator would be prior to it by an infinite duration.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for God's priority over the world by an infinite duration. The argument begins by stating that since God exists eternally (al-azal) and the world did not exist in eternity, God must be prior to the world. It then uses a thought experiment: suppose God existed one thousand years before the world, and also existed two thousand years before the world. The priority of two thousand years is greater in measure than that of one thousand years. This increase in priority is not merely a product of our assumption, because if it were merely assumed, it would change with different assumptions. But intuitively, the measure of priority of two thousand years is double that of one thousand years, and duration (al-mudda) and time (al-zaman) are nothing but this measurable, comparable quantity. Therefore, it follows that if the world is originated (hadith), God must precede it by an infinite duration, because there is no limit to how far back we can go.

Key Terms
الأزل
المدة
الزمان
التقدم
الحدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the argument only posits a finite duration, but the conclusion infers infinite duration.
Correction: The thought experiment with 1000 and 2000 years is used to show that priority is measurable. Since it can be extended without limit, the priority is infinite, not finite.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude from the thought experiment about one thousand and two thousand years?
A) God exists outside time.
B) If the world is created, God precedes it by an infinite duration.
C) The world is eternal.
D) Duration is not real.

Key Takeaway
The priority of God over the world is not a finite time but an infinite duration, as shown by the logical extension of measurable priority.

Refuting the Analogy of Temporal Priority
Sanusi refutes an analogy claiming divine priority is like temporal priority without duration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's priority over the world cannot be analogous to the priority of one time part over another without duration.

Core Idea
Temporal priority requires a prior moment; eternity has no prior moment.

This passage presents a subtle objection against the traditional understanding of God's precedence. An interlocutor argues that since parts of time can be prior to each other without any duration between them, God's priority over the world might be similar. Sanusi's answer exposes a critical flaw in this analogy, clarifying the unique nature of divine priority.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand the analogy being drawn: parts of time can be prior without duration, so why not God's priority?
The objector equates two different kinds of priority.
2
Identify Sanusi's response
Sanusi points out that the priority of time parts is based on the non-existence of the later part with the prior part.
3
Grasp the key distinction
This non-existence only makes sense if the prior part exists. In eternity, there are no time parts at all.
The analogy collapses because the condition for temporal priority is absent.
4
Reflect on the implication
This reinforces that God's priority is not temporal but a different kind of precedence—without any prior time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما قوله : ( لما جاز أن يتقدم بعض أجزاء الزمان على البعض الآخر ، لا بالمدة . فلم لا يجوز مثله في تقدم ذات الباري [ تعالى(۱) ] على أول العالم ؟ . قلنا : إنما صح [ قولنا (۲) ] إن هذا الجزء من الزمان ، متأخر عن الجزء الأول لانا نقول : [ هذا(۳) ] الجزء ما كان موجوداً مع الجزء (4) الأول . إلا أن هذا المعنى إنما يصح ، إذا كان الجزء الأول موجوداً . أما لو قلنا إنه ما حصل في الأزل شيء من أجزاء المدة والزمان ، امتنع القول بكون العالم متأخراً عن البارى . فظهر الفرق .
As for his saying: 'Since it is permissible for some parts of time to be prior to other parts, without [any] duration, why is it not permissible likewise in the priority of the essence of the Creator, exalted, over the beginning of the world?' We say: Our saying that this part of time is posterior to the first part is only correct because we say: This part did not exist with the first part. However, this meaning is only correct if the first part exists. But if we say that nothing of the parts of duration and time occurred in eternity, then it is impossible to say that the world is posterior to the Creator. So the difference becomes clear.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector argues: parts of time can be prior to each other without a duration (e.g., one moment is after another without an interval), so why can't God's priority over the world be like that—without a duration? The answer is that the priority of one time part over another is meaningful only because the prior part actually exists. If we say that there was nothing of time in eternity, then we cannot say that the world is posterior to God in the same way that one time part is posterior to another. The difference is that the priority of time parts depends on the existence of a prior part, whereas in God's case there is no prior time at all.

Key Terms
التقدم
المدة
الزمان
الأزل
الجزء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's priority is analogous to one moment being after another without a duration.
Correction: Temporal priority depends on the existence of a prior moment, but in eternity there are no moments, so the analogy fails.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the analogy between God's priority and the priority of time parts?
A) Because time parts are not real.
B) Because the priority of time parts requires a prior part to exist, which is absent in eternity.
C) Because duration is not applicable to God.
D) Because the objector is a philosopher.

Key Takeaway
God's priority over the world is not temporal; it is a priority of existence without any prior time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson shows that temporal priority requires a prior moment. Are there areas in your life where you assume God's actions or attributes are like created things, even subtly? How will you actively remind yourself of God's absolute transcendence?
?
If God's priority is not temporal, then your relationship with Him is not bound by time. How does this truth change the way you approach prayer, patience, or repentance? Commit to one change you will make today based on this.

Deferring the Objection on Time and Motion
Sanusi presents an objection and defers its answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi handles an objection about time and motion by deferring the full answer to a later discussion.

Core Idea
Some objections are best answered with patience and proper placement.

In the study of kalam, objections often arise that seem compelling at first glance. Sanusi presents one such objection here: how can time and motion be eternal if they require being preceded by something else? Rather than give a rushed response, he defers the full answer to a dedicated chapter. This teaches us the importance of systematic argumentation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the double colon after 'thālithan' – likely a typo, but it shows the objection is the third one.
2
Understand the logical structure of the objection
The objection has three parts: (1) essence of time/motion requires being preceded by another, (2) eternity negates being preceded, (3) combining them is impossible. Identify each part in the text.
3
Note the author's response
Sanusi says: 'We will answer this in the chapter on your proofs that motions have a beginning and an origin.' This is a deferral strategy.
Consider why he doesn't answer immediately – perhaps the full refutation requires arguments about the origination of motion.
4
Reflect on the validity of deferrals in arguments
Ask yourself: Is deferring an objection a sign of weakness or a strategic choice? Discuss how systematic works often postpone certain answers to later sections.
Compare this to modern academic writing where some issues are addressed 'in due course'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله ثالثاً : : ماهية الزمان والحركة ، تقتضي المسبوقية بالغير، والأزلية تنافي المسبوقية بالغير، والجمع بينهما: محال ، قلنا : سنجيب عن هذا الكلام في باب دلائلكم على أن للحركات أزلا (۱) وبداية .
And as for his third saying: 'The essence of time and motion necessitates being preceded by another, and eternality (al-azaliyya) negates being preceded by another, and combining them is impossible.' We said: We will answer this speech in the chapter on your proofs that motions have a beginning and an origin.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector argues that time and motion require being preceded by something else, but eternity (al-azaliyya) implies no prior, so eternal time and motion are impossible. The author does not provide an immediate detailed response but postpones the answer to a later chapter where the proofs for the beginning of motions are discussed. This is a deferral strategy.

Fifth Argument: Time Has No Beginning
Fifth proof that time has no beginning based on the nature of temporal events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that time has no beginning based on the necessary precedence of every originated event.

Core Idea
Every event has a before, so time is without a first moment.

This passage presents a concise rational argument for the beginninglessness of time. The author appeals to the clear testimony of reason that every originated event must be preceded by something, leading to an infinite regress. As you read, notice how the argument defines time itself as the measure of this before-and-after sequence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the compact style; the argument is only a few lines.
2
Identify the key claim
The author states that every originated event is preceded by either non-existence or existence. This is the fundamental premise. Understand why it seems rationally necessary.
3
Trace the logical implication
If every event has a preceding 'before', that 'before' itself is a moment that must also be preceded, leading to an infinite chain. The author concludes that time and duration are this chain, so they have no beginning.
Ask yourself: Could the chain stop at a first moment? The argument says no.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : إن صريح العقل يشهد بأنه لا حادث ، إلا ويحصل قبله ، إما عدم وإما وجود . فعلى هذا ، فكل حادث ، فقد حصل قبله قبل آخر ، لا إلى أول . ولا معنى للمدة والزمان إلا ذلك فالمدة لا أول لها
The fifth argument: Sound reason witnesses that there is no originated thing except that before it occurs there is either non-existence or existence. On this basis, every originated thing has before it a 'before' that is without a beginning. And there is no meaning of duration and time except that. So duration has no beginning.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This brief passage presents the fifth argument (al-ḥujjah al-khāmisah). It appeals to sound reason (ṣarīḥ al-ʿaql), which testifies that every originated event (ḥādith) is preceded by something—either non-existence or another event. This 'before' itself must be preceded by another 'before', and so on ad infinitum, resulting in an infinite regress of 'before' moments with no first beginning. Since time and duration are precisely the measure of this before-and-after sequence, time itself must have no beginning. The argument is succinct: the very concept of an originated thing implies an infinite chain of precedence, and time is that chain.

Key Terms
حادث (ḥādith)
عدم (ʿadam)
وجود (wujūd)
قبل (qabl)
مدة (muddah)
زمان (zamān)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An event could be preceded by nothing.
Correction: Sound reason shows that every event is necessarily preceded by either non-existence or existence, ensuring a temporal regress.

Checkpoint
According to the fifth argument, why does time have no beginning?
A) Because time is an illusion.
B) Because every event is preceded by another event or non-existence, leading to an infinite chain of 'before' moments.
C) Because God created time as an eternal dimension.
D) Because the world is eternal and requires no beginning.

Key Takeaway
Time has no beginning because every temporal event requires a preceding moment, leading to an endless chain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time has no beginning, then your entire life is a tiny flash in an endless ocean of moments. Does that make your actions feel insignificant, or does it amplify their eternal weight? How will you live differently today knowing that each moment is preceded by an infinite past and followed by an infinite future?
?
The argument forces you to accept an infinite regress of moments. But you, personally, will experience only a finite number of them. Are you investing your finite moments in what truly matters for the infinite? What is one thing you will change today to align your time with that reality?
?
You are a temporal being surrounded by an eternal timeline. Your choices echo into that eternity. What have you done today that will still matter in a billion years? If nothing, what will you do about it starting now?

Priority of Non-Existence as a Positive Attribute
Sanusi analyzes the priority of non-existence as a positive attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth argument's claim that priority and posteriority are positive attributes distinct from non-existence itself.

Core Idea
Priority is not the same as non-existence—it is an extra positive attribute.

The sixth argument aims to prove time's eternity by analyzing the priority of non-existence. Sanusi argues that before something exists, its non-existence has a priority that is not simply non-existence itself. This distinction is crucial for understanding how time is a real measure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Notice the logical flow: premise → analysis.
The passage is cut off at the end; the full conclusion is not here.
2
Identify the key distinction
The author says that priority/posteriority are not the same as non-existence because two non-existences can share essence but differ in priority. Find this distinction in the text.
Look for the phrase 'ليس نفس العدم' (not the same as non-existence).
3
Reflect on the implication
If priority is a positive attribute, it requires a real measure—time. Think about why this leads to time being eternal.
The lesson title suggests this conclusion, though the passage does not state it explicitly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : كل محدث ، فإنه مسبوق بعدمه ، وكل ما كان مسبوقاً بعدمه، كان عدمه سابقاً عليه. وكون ذلك العدم سابقاً عليه ليس نفس العدم لأن العدم السابق ، والعدم اللاحق يتشاركان ، في كون كل واحد منها عدما ، ويتخالفان في التقدم والتأخر فمفهوم التقدم والتأخر أمر زائد على العدم المحض ، فهما وصفان ثبوتيان
The sixth argument: Every originated thing (muḥdath) is preceded by its non-existence, and everything that is preceded by its non-existence, its non-existence is prior to it. And that non-existence being prior to it is not the same as non-existence itself, because the prior non-existence and the posterior non-existence share in that each is non-existence, but they differ in priority and posteriority. So the concept of priority and posteriority is something additional to pure non-existence; thus they are two positive attributes.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth argument (al-ḥujjah al-sādisah), though it appears to be cut off at the end of the page. The author begins by stating that every originated thing (muḥdath) is preceded by its own non-existence. This priority (sābiqiyya) of non-existence is not the same as non-existence itself, because the non-existence that precedes and the non-existence that would follow (if the thing perishes later) are both non-existence, yet they differ in priority and posteriority. Therefore, priority and posteriority are additional concepts (zā'id) beyond pure non-existence; they are positive attributes (ṣifāt thubūtiyya). The implication, which the argument would continue to explain, is that these positive attributes require a real measure, which is time. Hence, time must be pre-eternal to account for the priority of non-existence.

Key Terms
محدث (muḥdath)
مسبوق (masbūq)
عدم (ʿadam)
تقدم (taqaddum)
تأخر (taʾakhkhur)
وصف ثبوتي (ṣifah thubūtiyyah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the priority of non-existence is simply part of non-existence itself, i.e., that non-existence inherently has a temporal order.
Correction: The author argues that non-existence is pure absence, and temporal relations like priority and posteriority are additional concepts. Two non-existences can be identical as non-existence but differ in priority, so priority must be a separate positive attribute.

Checkpoint
Why is the priority of non-existence not the same as non-existence itself according to the sixth argument?
A) Because priority and posteriority are illusions.
B) Because two non-existences share the nature of non-existence but differ in priority, so priority is extra.
C) Because non-existence cannot have attributes.
D) Because priority is a negative concept.

Key Takeaway
Priority and posteriority are positive attributes distinct from non-existence, indicating the need for a real temporal measure like time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If priority is a positive attribute distinct from non-existence, consider that your own existence was preceded by a real state of non-existence with priority. Does this make you feel more dependent on the One who brought you from that state into existence? How will you live today to acknowledge that your existence is not a given but a gift sustained by a real power? Commit to one concrete action that expresses this dependence.
?
The passage argues that priority and posteriority are real, not just mental constructs. When you think about your own death, your future non-existence will also have posteriority, a real attribute. How does knowing that non-existence is not just an absence but carries real relational attributes affect your urgency to prepare for what comes after? What is one step you will take today to prepare for that state?

The Fifth Proof: Reason Testifies Time Has No Beginning
Sanusi's fifth proof for the beginninglessness of time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that time has no beginning, based on the nature of precedence and the definition of time.

Core Idea
Time is the chain of endless antecedents — and that chain has no first link.

This lesson presents a concise rational argument for the eternity of time. The author invokes pure reason to show that every event is preceded by another, and this endless succession is precisely what time is. Let's examine the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Let the argument flow naturally.
Notice how compact the proof is.
2
Identify the key premise
The proof begins with a statement about every accident: it is preceded by either non-existence or existence. Understand why this is a self-evident truth.
This premise is the foundation.
3
Follow the chain
From the premise, reason that each prior event itself has another prior, leading to an infinite regress with no first member.
This is the core logical step.
4
Connect time to the chain
The author identifies duration and time with this very chain of precedence. Grasp why this identification is made.
Time is not separate from the sequence.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Since the chain has no beginning, time has no beginning. Consider the implications.
This proof does not rely on physical observations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : إن صريح العقل يشهد بأنه لا حادث ، إلا ويحصل قبله ، إما عدم وإما وجود . فعلى هذا ، فكل حادث ، فقد حصل قبله قبل آخر ، لا إلى أول . ولا معنى للمدة والزمان إلا ذلك فالمدة لا أول لها.
The fifth proof: Verily, pure reason testifies that there is no accident (hadith) except that before it occurs either non-existence or existence. So upon this, every accident has occurred before it another before, without a first. And duration and time mean nothing other than that, so duration has no beginning.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is the fifth proof (al-hujjah al-khamisah) for the eternity of time. The author states that pure reason ('aql) testifies that every originated thing (hadith) is preceded by either non-existence or existence. From this, it follows that for any given event, there is always a preceding event, and this chain extends without a first member. The author then identifies this chain of precedence with time itself: duration and time are nothing other than this successive priority. Therefore, time has no beginning (la awwala laha). The proof is concise and relies on the intuitive idea that every event has a prior condition, leading to an infinite regress that defines time.

Key Terms
صريح العقل
حادث
المدة
الزمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time began with the creation of the universe.
Correction: The proof shows that time itself is defined by the endless chain of antecedents. If the universe had a beginning, there is still a prior non-existence, and that non-existence itself is part of the temporal chain. Thus time has no beginning, regardless of when events start.

Checkpoint
According to the fifth proof, what does pure reason testify about every accident?
A) That it is created by God.
B) That it is preceded by either non-existence or existence.
C) That it is temporal.
D) That it has a beginning.

Key Takeaway
Time is the series of endless antecedents — and that series has no beginning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are a hadith — an accident brought into existence from non-existence. If time stretches back without beginning, your few decades are a fleeting instant in an endless chain. Does this make you feel insignificant, or does it deepen your awe for the One who exists outside time? How will you use your brief moment today to seek His pleasure?
?
The proof says every accident is preceded by either non-existence or existence. Your very existence was preceded by non-existence. Where would you be if Allah had not willed you to be? Does this realization strip away any pretense of self-sufficiency? How will you express your total dependence on Him in your actions today?
?
Time's endlessness means the regret you carry from yesterday is part of an infinite sequence. You cannot go back, but you can turn to the Eternal. What is one sin or missed opportunity you will repent from now, knowing that time grants no second chance but His mercy does?

The Sixth Proof: Precedence Requires Time
Sixth proof: precedence as positive attribute needing substratum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that precedence is a positive attribute that necessitates the existence of beginningless time.

Core Idea
Precedence is a real attribute, not just non-existence, and demands a temporal foundation.

This passage presents the sixth proof for the eternity of time. The author argues that the fact that things are preceded by non-existence implies that precedence itself is a positive attribute, which cannot be a property of nothingness. Instead, it must inhere in something real, and that something is time itself. The proof is subtle but foundational for the Islamic theological position on time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the logical flow from the premise to the conclusion.
Pay attention to the distinction between non-existence and precedence.
2
Identify the key distinction
The author argues that prior and posterior non-existence are both non-existence, yet they differ in precedence and delay. This shows precedence is an additional concept.
This is the crucial move: precedence is not reducible to non-existence.
3
Understand the need for a substratum
Since precedence is a positive attribute, it must inhere in something to avoid infinite regress. That substratum is time, which is therefore beginningless.
The conclusion is that time is eternal, existing before every originated thing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : كل محدث ، فإنه مسبوق بعدمه ، وكل ما كان مسبوقاً بعدمه، كان عدمه سابقاً عليه. وكون ذلك العدم سابقاً عليه ليس نفس العدم لأن العدم السابق ، والعدم اللاحق يتشاركان ، في كون كل واحد منها عدما ، ويتخالفان في التقدم والتأخر فمفهوم التقدم والتأخر أمر زائد على العدم المحض ، فهما وصفان ثبوتيان متنافيان ولا بد من فرض شيء ، تلحقه هذه القبلية والبعدية لذاته ، قطعاً للتسلسل . وذلك الشيء هو الزمان . فقبل كل حادث : زمان لا اول له وهو المطلوب.
The sixth proof: Every originated thing is preceded by its non-existence, and everything that is preceded by its non-existence, its non-existence is prior to it. And that non-existence being prior to it is not the same as the non-existence itself, because the prior non-existence and the posterior non-existence share in each being non-existence, but differ in precedence and delay. So the concept of precedence and delay is something additional to pure non-existence, so they are two positive (thubutiyyan) and mutually exclusive attributes. And it is necessary to posit something that is characterized by this priorness and posteriorness in itself, to cut off infinite regress. And that thing is time. So before every accident there is time without beginning, and that is the desired conclusion.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is the sixth proof (al-hujjah al-sadisah). The author argues that every originated thing (muhdath) is preceded by its non-existence. The fact that this non-existence is prior to the originated thing is not the same as the non-existence itself, because two non-existences (prior and posterior) share the attribute of being non-existence but differ in being prior or posterior. This difference indicates that precedence (taqaddum) and delay (ta'akhkhur) are additional concepts beyond pure non-existence, and thus they are positive (thubutiyyan) attributes, not merely negative. Since these are attributes, they require a substratum (mahall) that bears them. To avoid an infinite regress of such attributes, we must posit something that inherently possesses priority and posteriority, and that thing is time (al-zaman). Therefore, before every accident there is beginningless time, which is the desired conclusion that time is eternal. The proof hinges on the idea that precedence is a real relation that demands a substrate.

Key Terms
المحدث
العدم
التقدم
التأخر
صفات ثبوتية
الزمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Precedence is merely a relation or a mental construct with no extra-mental reality.
Correction: The author argues that precedence is a positive attribute (sifa thubutiyya) that inheres in something real, namely time. It is not reducible to pure non-existence or a mental fiction.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that precedence is not simply the non-existence itself?
A) Because non-existence cannot be prior.
B) Because prior and posterior non-existences share the same essence but differ in relation.
C) Because precedence is a positive attribute.
D) Because non-existence is a privation.

Key Takeaway
The sixth proof establishes that precedence is a real attribute that must inhere in time, thereby proving that time is eternal and beginningless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof argues that precedence is a real attribute that cannot exist without time. In your life, what things do you treat as 'just a matter of time' that actually have real weight and require you to act? What does it mean that you cannot defer responsibility indefinitely?
?
If time is beginningless and created by God, then your time is a gift from an eternal Source. How does that change your view of a typical day? Are you spending your moments as if they are part of an endless chain or as precious loans that will be accounted for?
?
The proof distinguishes between non-existence and the positive attribute of precedence. Are there areas in your life where you confuse absence (e.g., of sin) with actual virtue (e.g., of righteousness)? How can you actively cultivate positive attributes instead of just avoiding negative ones?

Objection and Answer on Precedence and Delay
Objection with three arguments and the answer's opening.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three arguments against precedence and delay being positive attributes, and how the answer reframes the proof without that premise.

Core Idea
Precedence and delay are relational, requiring change, not necessarily positive attributes.

In this passage, an objector challenges the idea that precedence is a positive attribute, presenting three logical arguments. The response cleverly sidesteps the premise and shows that the proof can proceed without it. By studying this exchange, you'll see how kalam dialectic refines key concepts.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the three numbered arguments of the objector and the beginning of the answer.
The answer is cut off; focus on the argument structure.
2
Identify each objection's core point
The first objection says that if precedence were a positive attribute, it would inhere in non-existence. The second leads to infinite regress. The third makes the prior and posterior simultaneous.
All three aim to prove precedence is not an existing attribute.
3
Understand the answer's strategy
The answer does not directly counter these objections; instead, it claims the proof does not depend on precedence being a positive attribute. It redefines the issue around change and states.
This is a common dialectical move in kalam.
4
Reflect on the role of change
The answer asserts that precedence and delay are conceivable only with change. Without change, there is no past or future.
This shifts the discussion from attributes to the necessity of change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لا تسلم أن تقدم الشيء على غيره : صفة ثبوتية . ويدل عليه الأول : إنكم وصفتم عدم الشيء بكونه متقدماً على غيره . وصفة العدم أن تكون موجودة. وإلا لزم قيام الموجود بالمعدوم ، وهو محال الثاني : إن التقدم والتأخر لو كانا صفتين موجودتين ، لكانت تلك الصفة متأخرة أيضاً على عدمها ، فيلزم : أن تكون لتلك الصفة : صفة أخرى إلى غير النهاية ، دفعة واحدة . وهو محال الثالث : لو كان التقدم والتأخر صفتين موجودتين ، لكانا من مقولة المضاف . والمضافان يوجدان معاً. فالتقدم والتأخر يوجدان معاً ، فيلزم : كون المتقدم والمتأخر معاً ، وهو محال . وإذا ثبت أن التقدم والتأخر ، ليسا صفتين موجودتين ، لم يلزم افتقارهما إلى محل موجود . أجابوا عنه : بأنه لا حاجة بنا في هذا الدليل إلى بيان كون التقدم والتأخر صفتين موجودتين . بل يمكننا إثبات مطلوبنا مع قطع النظر عن هذه المقدمة وتقريره : إن التقدم والتأخر لا يعقل حصولهما ، إلا عند تبديل حالة بحالة ، وإلا عند تغيره من صفة إلى صفة . فإنه لو لم يحدث أمر من الأمور ، ولم تتعير من الأحوال ، لم يحصل هناك شيء يحكم عليه بأنه صار ماضياً ، ولا على شيء بكونه مستقبلاً . وذلك لأن الماضي هو الذي كان موجوداً ، ثم زال الآن . والمستقبل هو الذي يتوقع حضوره، وهو الآن لم يحضر . فالماضي حالة
If it is said: We do not grant that the precedence of a thing over another is a positive attribute. Evidence for this: First: You described the non-existence of a thing as being prior to another. But an attribute of non-existence cannot exist; otherwise it would entail the existence subsisting in non-existence, which is impossible. Second: If precedence and delay were two existing attributes, then that attribute would also be delayed with respect to its own non-existence, leading to another attribute ad infinitum, all at once, which is impossible. Third: If precedence and delay were two existing attributes, they would belong to the category of relation (al-mudaf). Relatives exist together, so precedence and delay would exist together, entailing that the prior and the posterior are simultaneous, which is impossible. And if it is established that precedence and delay are not existing attributes, then they do not require an existing substratum. They answered: We do not need in this proof to demonstrate that precedence and delay are existing attributes. Rather, we can prove our goal independently of this premise. Its elucidation: Precedence and delay cannot be conceived except when there is a change of state from one state to another, except when there is alteration from one attribute to another. For if nothing occurred and nothing changed, there would be nothing judged as having become past, nor anything as being future. That is because the past is what existed and then has now ceased. The future is what is expected to come and has not now arrived. So the past is a state...
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage presents an objection (i'tirad) and its answer (jawab) regarding the nature of precedence and delay. The objector denies that precedence is a positive (thubuti) attribute, using three arguments: (1) If it were positive, you would be ascribing an attribute to non-existence (since non-existence is described as prior), which is impossible because a positive attribute cannot inhere in non-existence. (2) If precedence were a positive attribute, it would itself be subject to precedence and delay, leading to an infinite regress of attributes. (3) Precedence and delay are relational (min qabilat al-mudaf); relatives exist simultaneously, so the prior and posterior would exist together, contradicting their definition. The objector concludes that precedence is not an existing attribute, so it does not need a substratum. The answer (ajabu 'anhu) counters that the original proof does not depend on showing that precedence and delay are existing attributes. Instead, the proof can be reformulated without that premise: the very conception of precedence and delay requires change (tabdil hal bi hal) and alteration (taghayyur min sifah ila sifah). Without change, no distinction between past and future exists. This shows that time is necessary for change, regardless of whether precedence is a positive attribute. The answer is cut off, but the point is that the proof still stands.

Key Terms
صفة ثبوتية
المضاف
التقدم
التأخر
الماضي
المستقبل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: For precedence to be a real concept, it must be a positive attribute inhering in a substance.
Correction: The answer shows that the reality of precedence and delay can be understood through the phenomenon of change, without requiring them to be positive attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the third argument of the objection, why can precedence and delay not be existing attributes?
A) Because they are not real.
B) Because they belong to the category of relation, and relatives exist together, which would make the prior and posterior simultaneous.
C) Because they are negative.
D) Because they require an infinite regress.

Key Takeaway
Precedence and delay are understood through change, not through positive attributes inhering in substances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often cling to past achievements or regrets as if they are permanent attributes of your identity. If precedence is only real through change, what does that mean for the weight you give to past moments? How can you release yourself from being defined by what has already changed?
?
The answer insists that without change, there is no past or future. Are there areas in your life where you resist change, hoping to freeze time? What would it cost you to embrace that change is necessary for any meaningful progression toward Allah?
?
When you look at your future, do you treat it as something that will simply 'arrive' passively, or do you see it as requiring active change from your present state? How does understanding that precedence and delay depend on change affect your sense of responsibility for the person you are becoming?

Priority and Posteriority: Not Real Attributes
Sanusi presents an objection and answer regarding priority/posteriority as attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dialectical argument that priority and posteriority are not positive attributes, and the answer that these concepts imply change and temporal succession.

Core Idea
Priority and posteriority are relational concepts, not real attributes—they depend on change.

In this passage, Sanusi presents a typical kalam objection and its answer within a larger argument about the nature of time and attributes. The objector argues that priority and posteriority cannot be positive attributes because they would lead to absurdities. The answer reframes the issue, showing that these concepts are only conceivable with change, thereby supporting the claim that events must have occurred before the first moment of time.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer as a unit
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Notice how the objection presents three distinct arguments, and the answer responds to the underlying premise rather than each argument individually.
The objection uses 'First... Second... Third...' to structure its case.
2
Identify the three arguments of the objection
Find each of the three arguments. The first claims that priority cannot be an attribute of non-existence. The second claims infinite regress if it were an attribute. The third claims that priority and posteriority would coexist, contradicting their nature.
3
Understand the answer's strategy
The answer does not disprove that priority/posteriority are attributes. Instead, it argues that we don't need them to be attributes to make the point. Priority/posteriority only make sense with change, so they imply temporal succession before the first moment.
This reframes the debate from ontology to conceptual dependence.
4
See how the answer supports the larger argument
The key is that priority/posteriority before the first moment of time would mean events occurred before that moment, contradicting its being the first. Thus, the answer strengthens the claim that time had a beginning.
The overall context is about the priority of Allah's attributes or creation.
5
Reflect on the dialectical method
Notice that the answer does not reject the objection's premises entirely but shows that the objection's conclusion does not follow. This is a common kalam technique: accepting the objection's reasoning but denying its relevance.
The phrase 'لا حاجة بنا في هذا الدليل' signals the shift.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لا تسلم أن تقدم الشيء على غيره : صفة ثبوتية . ويدل عليه الأول : إنكم وصفتم عدم الشيء بكونه متقدماً على غيره . وصفة العدم أن تكون موجودة. وإلا لزم قيام الموجود بالمعدوم ، وهو محال الثاني : إن التقدم والتأخر لو كانا صفتين موجودتين ، لكانت تلك الصفة متأخرة أيضاً على عدمها ، فيلزم : أن تكون لتلك الصفة : صفة أخرى إلى غير النهاية ، دفعة واحدة . وهو محال الثالث : لو كان التقدم والتأخر صفتين موجودتين ، لكانا من مقولة المضاف . والمضافان يوجدان معاً. فالتقدم والتأخر يوجدان معاً ، فيلزم : كون المتقدم والمتأخر معاً ، وهو محال . وإذا ثبت أن التقدم والتأخر ، ليسا صفتين موجودتين ، لم يلزم افتقارهما إلى محل موجود . أجابوا عنه : بأنه لا حاجة بنا في هذا الدليل إلى بيان كون التقدم والتأخر صفتين موجودتين . بل يمكننا إثبات مطلوبنا مع قطع النظر عن هذه المقدمة وتقريره : إن التقدم والتأخر لا يعقل حصولهما ، إلا عند تبديل حالة بحالة ، وإلا عند تغيره من صفة إلى صفة . فإنه لو لم يحدث أمر من الأمور ، ولم تتعير من الأحوال ، لم يحصل هناك شيء يحكم عليه بأنه صار ماضياً ، ولا على شيء بكونه مستقبلاً . وذلك لأن الماضي هو الذي كان موجوداً ، ثم زال الآن . والمستقبل هو الذي يتوقع حضوره، وهو الآن لم يحضر . فالماضي والمستقبل والحال لا يتقرر مفهوماتهم إلا عند وجود بعد عدم ، أو عدم بعد وجود . فلما ثبت حصول معنى القبلية والبعدية قبل أول الزمان ، علمنا : أن حدوث الحوادث كان حاصلا قبل ذلك الأول . وهذا يناقض كون ذلك الأول : أولاً . والله أعلم
If it is said: We do not concede that the priority of a thing over another is a positive attribute. Evidence for this: First: You described the non-existence of a thing as being prior to another. But an attribute of non-existence cannot be existent. Otherwise an existent would subsist in a non-existent, which is impossible. Second: If priority and posteriority were existent attributes, then that attribute would also be posterior to its own non-existence, leading to an infinite regress of attributes at once, which is impossible. Third: If priority and posteriority were existent attributes, they would belong to the category of relation, and the two relatives exist together. Thus priority and posteriority would exist together, requiring the prior and the posterior to be together, which is impossible. And if it is established that priority and posteriority are not existent attributes, then they do not require an existent substrate. They answered: We do not need in this proof to demonstrate that priority and posteriority are existent attributes. Rather we can establish our claim regardless of this premise. Its formulation: Priority and posteriority are not conceivable except with a change from state to state, or alteration from attribute to attribute. For if nothing occurred and no states changed, there would be nothing judged as having become past, nor anything as future. That is because the past is that which existed and then ceased, and the future is that which is expected to arrive and has not yet arrived. Thus the past, future, and present are not determined in their concepts except with existence after non-existence or non-existence after existence. Since the meaning of priority and posteriority is established before the first moment of time, we know that the occurrence of events took place before that first moment. This contradicts that first moment being first. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer regarding the nature of priority and posteriority. The objector argues that priority and posteriority are not positive (thubutiyya) attributes, giving three proofs: First, if they were attributes, they would describe non-existence, but an attribute of non-existence cannot exist. Second, if they existed, each would require another attribute ad infinitum. Third, they would be relative terms requiring simultaneous existence, contradiction. The answer (ajaba) refutes the need to prove they are attributes; instead, priority/posteriority are only conceivable with change, thus indicating temporal succession. Since priority exists before the first moment, events must have occurred before that moment, contradicting its being first. The argument assumes that before any event there is time, and that priority/posteriority imply change and hence temporality.

صفة ثبوتية
عدم
مضاف

بعدية
أول الزمان

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Priority and posteriority are real, positive attributes that exist in time itself.
Correction: The passage shows that priority and posteriority are relational concepts dependent on change, not inherent attributes. The objection tries to deny they are attributes at all, but the answer shows they are meaningful only with change.

Checkpoint

B) They would belong to the category of relation, requiring simultaneous existence of prior and posterior.
C) They cannot describe non-existence.
D) They are not known to the intellect.

Key Takeaway
Priority and posteriority are not independent attributes; they are only conceivable with change, which supports the argument that time had a beginning.

The answer uses the concept of priority before the first moment to prove time had a beginning. If your life is a series of moments, what does it mean that you exist in a time that began? Does that change how you view the urgency of your obedience to the Creator of time?

The Distinctness of Azal and Abad Proves Duration Has No Beginning
Rational enumeration proof of duration's beginninglessness from concept distinctness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that duration (al-muddah) has no beginning, based on the distinctness of the concepts of pre-eternity (al-azal) and post-eternity (al-abad).

Core Idea
The distinct concepts of azal and abad show that duration has no beginning.

This passage presents the seventh proof that duration has no beginning. The author argues by analyzing the concepts of pre-eternity (azal) and post-eternity (abad) as applied to God. By showing they are rationally distinct and not identical to God's essence, he establishes that duration itself is eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with focus on the argument structure
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author begins with an agreed premise, then uses reason to show the distinction between two concepts, and builds toward a conclusion about duration.
2
Understand the premise and the distinction
The author starts: 'There is no doubt that God was existing in azal and will be existing in abad.' Then he asks whether the two concepts are distinct. Read how he proves they are distinct by reductio ad absurdum.
Pay attention to the phrase 'بديهة العقل' (first principles of reason).
3
Follow the proof that they are distinct from God's essence
Since God is qualified by existence, and existence with azal is not the same as existence with abad, each concept must be something other than God's essence. The author also shows they are distinct from the concept of the world's non-existence.
4
Learn the definitions of azal and abad
Azal is defined as 'everlastingness with no beginning in the past' and abad as 'everlastingness with no end in the future.' These are the meanings of duration, time, and eternity.
The terms al-muddah, al-dahr, and al-sarmad are used synonymously here.
5
Conclude that duration has no beginning
The author concludes that since these concepts are real and distinct, duration (which is what they describe) must have no beginning. This completes the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : لا شك أنه يصدق على ذات الله تعالى : أنه كان موجوداً في الأزل ، وأنه سيكون موجوداً في الأبد . فهل يتميز في حقه : مفهوم أنه كان موجوداً في الأزل ، عن مفهوم أنه موجود أو سيكون في لا يزال ، أو لا يتميز ؟ وهذا القسم الثاني : باطل في بديهة العقل ، لأنه إن لم يتميز أحد المفهومين عن الثاني ، لكان المفهوم من هذين الكلامين مفهوماً واحداً ، ولكان التعبير عنه بهذين اللفظين : محض في العبارة. وبديهة العقل : حاكمة بأنه ليس كذلك . فإن المفهوم من قولنا : كان في الأزل : إشارة إلى الماضي . والمفهوم من قولنا : سيكون في لا يزال : إشارة إلى المستقبل . ولو غيرنا العبارة ، وقلنا : إنه كان في المستقبل ، وسيكون في الماضي ، فإن صريح العقل يشهد بفساده . فعلمنا : أن التغاير بين هذين المفهومين : حاصل في بديهة العقل . إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : إنه تعالى : محكوم عليه بالوجود . والحصول مع كل واحد من هذين المفهومين لكن واحداً من هذين المفهومين : غير محكوم عليه بالحصول ، مع المفهوم الآخر . وذلك يوجب كون كل واحد من هذين المفهومين مغايراً لذات الله تعالى. وأيضاً : فهما مغايران للمفهوم من كون العالم معدوماً ، فإن المفهوم من العدم ، يمكن تعقله الأزل تارة ، ومع الأبد أخرى . فيثبت : أن المفهوم من الأزل، وأن المفهوم من الأبد : أمر مغاير لذات الله تعالى ، ولعدم العالم . بل المفهوم من الأزل : دوام لا أول له في طرفي الماضي. والمفهوم من الأبد : دوام لا آخر له في المستقبل . وهذان الأمران مغايران لذات الله تعالى ، ولعدم العالم . ولا معنى للمدة والدهـر والسرمد إلا ذلك . فيثبت : أنه لا أول للدهر والمدة
The seventh proof: There is no doubt that it is true of God most high that He was existing in pre-eternity (al-azal) and that He will be existing in post-eternity (al-abad). So is the concept that He was existing in pre-eternity distinguished in His case from the concept that He is or will be existing in 'la yazal' (endless future) or not? And this second division is invalid by the first principles of reason (badihah al-aql), because if one of the two concepts is not distinguished from the other, then the conception from these two statements would be one conception, and the expression for them by these two expressions would be pure verbal variation. And the first principles of reason judge that it is not so. For the conception from our saying 'was in pre-eternity' is an indication of the past, and the conception from our saying 'will be in la yazal' is an indication of the future. And if we changed the expression and said: He was in the future and will be in the past, then clear reason testifies to its falsity. So we know that the distinction between these two concepts is obtained in the first principles of reason. If this is established, then we say: He most high is qualified by existence. And existence together with each one of these two concepts is not qualified by existence together with the other concept. And that necessitates that each one of these two concepts is other than (mugayir) the essence of God most high. Also, they are other than the concept of the world being non-existent, for the concept of non-existence can be conceived in relation to pre-eternity sometimes and with post-eternity at other times. So it is established that the concept of pre-eternity and the concept of post-eternity is something other than God's essence and other than the non-existence of the world. Rather, the concept of pre-eternity is everlastingness with no beginning in the direction of the past, and the concept of post-eternity is everlastingness with no end in the future. And these two things are other than God's essence and other than the non-existence of the world. And there is no meaning to 'al-muddah' (duration) and 'al-dahr' (time) and 'al-sarmad' (eternity) except that. So it is established that there is no beginning for time (al-dahr) and duration (al-muddah).
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is the seventh proof that duration (al-muddah) and time (al-dahr) have no beginning. The proof is based on the rational analysis of the concepts of pre-eternity (al-azal) and post-eternity (al-abad) as applied to God's existence. The argument proceeds as follows: 1. It is agreed that God was existing in pre-eternity and will be existing in post-eternity. 2. The concepts of 'was in pre-eternity' and 'will be in post-eternity' are distinct in the mind. This is evident because if they were the same concept, then saying 'He was in the future' would be equivalent to 'He will be in the past', which is false. Reason clearly distinguishes them. 3. Since God is qualified by existence, and existence is associated with each distinct concept, but the association with one concept is not the same as with the other, therefore each concept must be different from God's essence. They are also different from the concept of the world's non-existence, because non-existence can be thought of in relation to pre-eternity or post-eternity. 4. The concepts of pre-eternity and post-eternity are defined as everlastingness without beginning in the past and everlastingness without end in the future respectively. These two concepts are distinct from God's essence and from the non-existence of the world. 5. The terms 'muddah', 'dahr', and 'sarmad' refer exactly to these concepts. Therefore, duration (muddah) and time (dahr) have no beginning.

Correction: The argument shows that 'azal' is a distinct concept referring to everlastingness without beginning, and it is not the same as God's essence or the non-existence of the world.

Key Takeaway

Proof That Duration Is an Eternal Condition
The argument distinguishes 'God was with non-existence' from 'God will be with non-existence', proving a special condition that is duration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the phrase 'God was with non-existence' implies a special condition (duration) that is eternal and not reducible to mere existence and non-existence.

Core Idea
The word 'was' carries a modal condition that reveals duration as an eternal reality.

This lesson examines the eighth proof from Al-Matalib al-Aliyah, which uncovers a subtle logical point about time itself. By comparing 'God was with non-existence' to 'God will be with non-existence', the argument shows that 'was' implies a special condition beyond just two things existing together. That condition is what we call duration, and it turns out to be timeless.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the logical flow: a conditional, two possible interpretations, a rejection, and a conclusion.
The argument is concise; pay attention to how 'will be' is used as a counterexample.
2
Identify the two interpretations of 'was'
The passage presents two possibilities for what 'was' means in 'God was with non-existence'. Locate both and understand why the first is rejected.
3
Understand the rejection via 'will be'
The first interpretation is rejected because 'God will be with non-existence' would then mean the same thing, which is false. Grasp why this counterexample works.
4
See how the second interpretation leads to duration
The second interpretation introduces a special condition. That condition is shown to be eternal, and it is identified as duration (al-muddah). Connect this to the lesson's objective.
Note that 'duration' here is not time itself but the condition that underlies temporal statements.
5
Test your understanding with the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to check if you can identify the flaw in the first interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة : لو كان العالم حادثاً ، لصدق قولنا : إنه تعالى كان موجوداً مع عدم العالم. والمفهوم من قولنا : ( كان ) : إما أن يكون هو وجود البارى تعالى وعدم العالم فقط . أو المفهوم منه هذان الأمران ، بشرط خاص وكيفية خاصة . والأول باطل لأن قولنا : سيكون البارىء موجوداً مع عدم العالم ؛ قد حصل فيه وجود البارى، وعدم العالم ، مع أنه لم يحصل منه ما هو المفهوم من قولنا : كان البارى مع عدم العالم . فيثبت : أن قولنا : كان الباريء مع عدم العالم : إشارة إلى وجود البارى، وعدم العالم ، بشرط خاص وكيفية خاصة . ولا شك أن ذلك الشرط ، وتلك الكيفية : أمر دائم من الأزل إلى الآن. ولا معنى للمدة والزمان إلا ذلك المفهوم
The eighth proof: If the world were originated, then our saying 'God most high was existing with the non-existence of the world' would be true. And the concept from our saying 'was' (kāna) is either just the existence of the Creator (al-bāri') and the non-existence of the world only, or the concept from it is these two matters with a special condition and a special modality. And the first is invalid because our saying 'the Creator will be existing with the non-existence of the world' includes the existence of the Creator and the non-existence of the world, yet it does not include that which is the concept from our saying 'the Creator was with the non-existence of the world'. So it is established that our saying 'the Creator was with the non-existence of the world' is an indication of the existence of the Creator and the non-existence of the world, with a special condition and a special modality. And there is no doubt that that condition and that modality is an eternal matter from pre-eternity to now. And there is no meaning to duration (al-muddah) and time (al-zaman) except that concept.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth proof showing that duration (al-muddah) is an eternal condition. The argument begins with a conditional: if the world is originated, then it is true to say 'God was existing with the non-existence of the world.' The author then analyzes the concept of 'was' (kāna) in this statement. Two possibilities are considered: either the concept of 'was' is simply the combination of God's existence and the world's non-existence, without any additional condition; or it includes a special condition and modality. The first possibility is rejected by a counterexample: the statement 'God will be existing with the non-existence of the world' also contains the same two elements (God's existence and the world's non-existence), but it does not convey the same meaning as 'was'. Therefore, 'was' must include an additional condition. This condition is the temporal relation of pastness. Since this condition has been true from pre-eternity until now, it is an eternal matter. And this condition is precisely what is meant by duration (al-muddah) and time (al-zaman). Thus, duration is an eternal reality that has always existed.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'was' simply denotes past existence without any additional condition.
Correction: The argument shows that 'was' implies a modal condition of pastness that is not reducible to the mere fact of existence and non-existence, as demonstrated by the different meaning of 'will be'.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'God was with non-existence' contains a special condition—duration—which is eternal and cannot be reduced to mere coexistence.

What needs to change in your daily routine for you to truly live sub specie aeternitatis (under the aspect of eternity)?

Duration Cannot Begin: The Definition of Origination
Proof that time cannot have a beginning using the definition of origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why duration cannot have a beginning or end, based on the definition of origination and the impossibility of a time before time.

Core Idea
Time cannot be originated because origination itself requires a time before time.

In this passage, the author presents a powerful rational proof that time cannot have a beginning. The proof hinges on the very definition of what it means for something to be originated (muhdath). By carefully analyzing this definition, we see that applying it to time leads to an absurdity: the need for a time before time. This proof is a classic example of how rational arguments in Islamic theology establish necessary truths about creation and eternity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice how the argument begins with a definition of 'originated'.
Focus on the logical flow from definition to conclusion.
2
Understand the logical structure
Follow the argument: if time is originated, then before it existed, there must have been a time in which it did not exist. That preceding time is itself time, so time would have to exist before itself—a contradiction.
This is the core of the proof.
3
Apply the same reasoning to the future
The proof concludes that the same reasoning applies to the future: duration cannot have an end either. Reflect on why any limit on time leads to a paradox.
The argument is symmetric for past and future.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة : إن صريح العقل يشهد بأنه لا مفهوم من كون الشيء محدثاً ، إلا أن نقول : إن ذلك الشيء ما كان موجوداً في الوقت المتقدم ، ثم صار موجوداً فلو حكمنا على الزمان : بكونه محدثاً. لكان معنى كونه محدثاً : أنه ما كان موجوداً في الوقت المتقدم ، ثم صار موجوداً وهذا يقتضي : أن الوقت والزمان كان موجوداً ، قبل أن كان موجوداً . وهو محال . لان كل ما أفضى فرض عدمه إلى فرض وجوده ، كان فرض عدمه محالاً . وهذا الدليل كما تقرر في جانب الأول ، فهو بعينه قائم في جانب الآخر . فالمدة تمتنع أن يحصل لها أول وآخر .
The ninth proof: Clear reason testifies that there is no concept of a thing being originated (muhdath) except that we say that that thing was not existing in the preceding time, then it became existing. So if we judged that time (al-zaman) is originated, then the meaning of its being originated would be that it was not existing in the preceding time, then it became existing. And this necessitates that time and time was existing before it was existing, which is impossible. For everything whose supposition of its non-existence leads to the supposition of its existence, the supposition of its non-existence is impossible. And this proof, as it is established on the side of the first (i.e., the past), is exactly valid on the side of the other (the future). So duration (al-muddah) is impossible to have a beginning and an end.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth proof that duration (al-muddah) cannot have a beginning or an end. The proof uses the definition of origination (al-huduth). Something is originated if it did not exist in a preceding time and then came into existence. Now suppose time itself were originated. Then according to the definition, time would have to be preceded by a time in which it did not exist, and then it came to be. But that preceding time would itself be time, so we would have time before time, which is contradictory. Therefore, it is impossible for time to be originated. The same argument applies to the future: duration cannot have an end. Any hypothetical limit leads to the supposition of something beyond it. The proof concludes that duration is necessarily eternal without beginning or end.

Key Terms
الحدوث
الزمان
المدة
العدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that time could have a beginning without a preceding time, simply by starting at a first moment.
Correction: The definition of origination itself requires a preceding time in which the thing did not exist. So if time began, there must have been a time before it, which is contradictory.

Checkpoint
According to the ninth proof, why cannot time be originated?
A) Because time is uncreated
B) Because origination requires a preceding time, leading to a contradiction
C) Because God cannot create time
D) Because time is an illusion

Key Takeaway
Duration cannot have a beginning because the definition of origination would require a time before time, leading to an impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The proof shows that the concept of 'beginning' cannot apply to time. In your daily life, you often think of past and future. Which of your sins do you rely on time to erase, forgetting that time itself is not a healer but a creation of Allah? Will you turn to the One who is beyond time for forgiveness?
?
If duration cannot have an end, then your soul will continue eternally. Does this reality make you fear the consequences of your present choices? What is one action today that you will change because you truly believe time is going somewhere without a final stop?

The Ninth Argument: The Impossibility of Originating Time
Rāzi argues that origination implies time, answers objection about infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi argues that the concept of origination (ḥudūth) necessarily implies prior time, thereby proving that time itself cannot be originated, and how he refutes the objection that origination does not require a temporal framework.

Core Idea
The concept of origination inherently implies prior time, so time cannot be originated.

Al-Razi presents the ninth proof for the eternity of time, starting with a conceptual analysis of what it means for something to be originated. He argues that the very notion of origination presupposes a prior temporal moment, leading to the conclusion that time itself cannot be originated without absurdity. He then addresses an objection that tries to strip origination of its temporal implication, and his response reveals how deeply time is embedded in our reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the opening argument where Razi sets out the concept of origination and applies it to time. Notice the logical structure: if time were originated, it would require a prior time.
Pay attention to the phrase ' لا مفهوم من كون الشيء محدثاً إلا أن نقول...'
2
Identify the objection
The opponents deny that origination requires a prior time; they say it only means 'it did not exist, then existed.' Consider the infinite regress argument they offer.
The objection claims that insisting on a prior time leads to an infinite chain.
3
Analyze the refutation
Razi responds by showing that even the words 'kāna' and 'thumma' imply temporal sequence. The intellect cannot conceive of origination without continuous duration.
He argues that the very language of non-existence and existence is temporal.
4
Reflect on the regress argument
Razi turns the infinite regress objection back to show that it actually supports his position: the need for a prior part for each temporal part confirms time's eternity.
He says 'وهكذا نقول' (we say the same).
5
Connect to innate intuitions
Note that Razi appeals to badā’ih al-‘uqūl (innate dispositions of the intellect) as the foundation for the necessity of time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة : إن صريح العقل يشهد بأنه لا مفهوم من كون الشيء محدثاً ، إلا أن نقول : إن ذلك الشيء ما كان موجوداً في الوقت المتقدم ، ثم صار موجوداً . فلو حكمنا على الزمان : بكونه محدثاً. لكان معنى كونه محدثاً : أنه ما كان موجوداً في الوقت المتقدم ، ثم صار موجوداً . وهذا يقتضي : أن الوقت والزمان كان موجوداً ، قبل أن كان موجوداً . وهو محال . لان كل ما أفضى فرض عدمه إلى فرض وجوده ، كان فرض عدمه محالاً . وهذا الدليل كما تقرر في جانب الأول ، فهو بعينه قائم في جانب الآخر . فالمدة تمتنع أن يحصل لها أول وآخر . فإن قالوا : لا نسلم أن المعقول من الحدوث : هو أنه ما كان موجوداً في الوقت المتقدم ، ثم صار موجوداً . بل نقول : المعقول من الحدوث : أنه ما كان موجوداً ، ثم صار موجوداً من غير حاجة إلى تقرير مدة ، وفرض زمان . والدليل على صحة ما ذكرنا : أنه لو كان الأمر كما ذكرتم ، لزم أن يفتقر حدوث كل واحد من أجزاء الزمان، إلى زمان آخر ، إلى غير النهاية . وهو محال . والجواب : إن قول القائل : إنه ما كان موجوداً : ثم صار موجوداً صريح في إثبات الزمان . لأن قولنا : ( كان ) : لفظ يدل على الماضي ولا يتصور العقل من الماضي ، إلا أمر من الأمور ، كان حاضراً ثم انقضى . وأيضاً لفظ ( ثم ) : يدل على حصول شيء ، بعد حصول شيء آخر . وكل هذه الألفاظ : تدل على أن العقل لا يمكنه أن يتصور معنى الحدوث البتة ، إلا بعد فرض مدة مستمرة ، و زمان دائم. فإن قالوا : فهذا تمسك بمجرد الألفاظ . فنقول : ليس الأمر هذا تنبيه على أن العقل لا يمكنه أن يتلفظ بلفظ، ولا أن يشير إلى معنى معقول ، إلا ويقرن حدوثه بزمان ، ويقرن عدمه السابق بزمان . وذلك يدل على أن الإقرار بدوام المدة ووجودها من الأزل إلى الأبد : مركوز في بدائه العقول . وأما قوله : ( كان يلزم افتقار حدوث كل واحد من أجزاء الزمان ، إلى زمان آخر ، إلى غير النهاية : فنقول : وهكذا نقول ، لأنه لولا أن الجزء السابق كان موجوداً ، وإلا لامتنع أن يحكم على الجزء المتأخر : بكونه حادثاً متأخراً . والله أعلم
The ninth proof: Indeed, clear reason testifies that there is no concept of a thing being originated (muḥdath) except that we say: that thing did not exist in the prior time, then it came into existence. So if we judge time to be originated, the meaning of its being originated would be that it did not exist in the prior time, then it came into existence. And this necessitates that time and moment existed before it existed. That is impossible. For everything whose supposition of non-existence leads to the supposition of its existence, its supposition of non-existence is impossible. This proof, just as it is established on the one side, is equally established on the other side. Thus duration is impossible to have a beginning and an end. Then they said: We do not accept that the intelligible of origination is that it did not exist in the prior time, then it came into existence. Rather, we say: the intelligible of origination is that it did not exist, then it came into existence, without need to establish a duration or suppose a time. The proof of the validity of what we have mentioned is that if it were as you have said, then the origination of every single part of time would require another time, ad infinitum, which is impossible. The answer: Indeed, the statement of the one who says 'it did not exist, then it came into existence' is explicit in establishing time. Because our saying 'kāna' (was) is a word indicating the past, and the intellect does not conceive of the past except as something that was present and then elapsed. Also, the word 'thumma' (then) indicates the occurrence of something after the occurrence of another thing. All these words indicate that the intellect cannot conceive of the meaning of origination at all except after supposing a continuous duration and perpetual time. If they say: This is merely clinging to words. We say: It is not so; this is a notification that the intellect cannot utter a word or indicate an intelligible meaning without associating its origination with time and associating its prior non-existence with time. That indicates that the acknowledgment of the perpetuity of duration and its existence from pre-eternity to post-eternity is ingrained in the innate dispositions of intellects. As for his statement: 'It would necessitate that the origination of every part of time requires another time, ad infinitum,' we say: We say the same, because if the prior part were not existent, then it would be impossible to judge the posterior part as being originated and posterior. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is the ninth proof (al-ḥujja al-tāsi‘a) for the eternity of time, followed by an objection and answer. The proof begins by asserting that the concept of something being originated (muḥdath) necessarily implies that it did not exist in a prior time and then came into existence. If we apply this to time itself, we would have to say that time did not exist in a prior time, which would require a time before time—an absurdity. Therefore, time cannot be originated; it must be eternal. The author then presents an objection from opponents: they argue that the intelligible meaning of origination is simply 'it did not exist, then it existed' without needing to posit a prior time. They claim that if we insist on a prior time, an infinite regress would follow. The answer is that even the phrase 'it did not exist, then it existed' implicitly involves the concept of past time, because the words 'kāna' (was) and 'thumma' (then) are temporal. The intellect cannot conceive of origination without presupposing a continuous duration. Thus, the acknowledgment of eternal duration is innate (makrūz fī badā’ih al-‘uqūl). Regarding the infinite regress objection, the author accepts it but turns it around: the regress is precisely what proves the necessity of a prior part for every temporal part, hence time's eternity.

Key Terms
حدوث (ḥudūth)
محدث (muḥdath)
زمان (zamān)
كان (kāna)
ثم (thumma)
مدة (mudda)
بدائه العقول (badā’ih al-‘uqūl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the concept of origination can be understood without any reference to time, as simply 'it did not exist, then it existed.'
Correction: Razi shows that even this minimal expression involves temporal language ('kāna' and 'thumma' imply past time and sequence), so time is inextricably linked to origination.

Checkpoint

D) By arguing that time is a mental construct.

Key Takeaway
The concept of origination necessarily implies preceding time, therefore time itself cannot be originated.

?
Rāzi claims that acknowledgment of perpetual time is ingrained in your intellect. When you sense that something is 'past' or 'future,' do you realize you are implicitly affirming an uncreated dimension? Does that humble you, or do you take it for granted?
